\section{Master Theorem Chain for the Standard-Model-Type Infrared Structure in TECT}

\subsection{Purpose}

In this section we collect the structural results obtained in the previous sections into a single theorem chain.
The goal is not to claim more than what has actually been established, but to state precisely which parts of the TECT construction are already mathematically organized and how they fit together.

The central claim is that, under a finite set of clearly stated hypotheses, the BCC topological energy condensate admits an infrared sector with the following properties:

\[
\text{BCC selection}
\Longrightarrow
\mathbb{CP}^2 \text{ internal geometry}
\Longrightarrow
S(U(3)\times U(2))
\Longrightarrow
SU(3)_c\times SU(2)_L\times U(1)_Y
\]
\[
\Longrightarrow
\text{chiral defect families}
\Longrightarrow
\text{anomaly cancellation}
\Longrightarrow
N_{\mathrm{gen}}=3
\Longrightarrow
\text{hierarchy and mixing}
\Longrightarrow
\text{IR isotropy and emergent Lorentz symmetry}.
\]

We now formulate this chain rigorously.

\subsection{Hypotheses}

We separate the assumptions into ultraviolet, geometric, and infrared hypotheses.

\paragraph{(H1) BCC ultraviolet selection.}
The ultraviolet condensate is selected by the exact quartic additive resonance extremum of the cuboctahedral 12-vector star
\[
S_{\mathrm{BCC}}
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt 2}
\{(\pm1,\pm1,0),(\pm1,0,\pm1),(0,\pm1,\pm1)\},
\]
with exact additive resonance count
\[
\Lambda_{\mathrm{BCC}}
=
\sum_v r(v)^2
=
540,
\qquad
r(v)=\#\{(a,b)\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\times S_{\mathrm{BCC}}:a+b=v\}.
\]
Thus the BCC phase is selected as the quartic-resonance extremizer.

\paragraph{(H2) Internal orientational geometry.}
The low-energy orientational order parameter is projective:
\[
z(x)\in \mathbb C^3,
\qquad
z^\dagger z=1,
\qquad
z\sim e^{i\alpha(x)}z,
\]
so that the physical internal field is valued in
\[
\mathbb{CP}^2 \cong SU(3)/(SU(2)\times U(1)).
\]

\paragraph{(H3) Defect localization and adiabatic reduction.}
There exists a localized defect sector for which the full defect Dirac operator admits a normalizable transverse mode, so that the low-energy internal zero-mode problem reduces to the \(\mathbb{CP}^2\) geometry.

\paragraph{(H4) Minimal positive quantization level.}
The defect moduli space \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{def}}\cong \mathbb{CP}^2\) carries a Berry/WZW symplectic form
\[
\Omega=k\,\omega_{\mathrm{FS}},
\qquad k\in \mathbb Z_{>0},
\]
and the physically realized minimal chiral defect corresponds to the first positive level
\[
k=1.
\]

\paragraph{(H5) Infrared isotropic fixed point.}
The low-energy TECT soft sector is governed by an isotropic infrared fixed point continuously connected to the \(O(N_{\mathrm{eff}})\) Wilson--Fisher-type fixed point, with conservative effective component number
\[
N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6.
\]

These hypotheses will be explicitly referenced below.

\subsection{Theorem A: BCC selection and ultraviolet phase}

\paragraph{Theorem A.}
Under hypothesis \textnormal{(H1)}, the ultraviolet condensate is selected in the BCC phase by exact quartic additive resonance extremization.

\paragraph{Proof.}
Define the additive resonance functional
\[
\Lambda(S)=\sum_v r(v)^2,
\qquad
r(v)=\#\{(a,b)\in S\times S:\ a+b=v\}.
\]
For the cuboctahedral 12-vector star \(S_{\mathrm{BCC}}\), explicit combinatorial enumeration yields
\[
\Lambda(S_{\mathrm{BCC}})=540.
\]
Thus the BCC shell is not introduced phenomenologically but selected by an exact quartic-resonance invariant.
\qed

\subsection{Theorem B: Internal \(\mathbb{CP}^2\) geometry}

\paragraph{Theorem B.}
Under hypothesis \textnormal{(H2)}, the infrared orientational sector is valued in \(\mathbb{CP}^2\), and the natural internal geometry is K\"ahler with Fubini--Study class \(h\in H^2(\mathbb{CP}^2,\mathbb Z)\).

\paragraph{Proof.}
The normalized complex vector \(z\in \mathbb C^3\) modulo local phase defines a projective line \([z]\in \mathbb{CP}^2\).
Hence the physical field is the rank-one projector
\[
P=zz^\dagger,
\qquad
P^2=P,\quad P^\dagger=P,\quad \mathrm{Tr}\,P=1,
\]
and the target space is
\[
\mathbb{CP}^2 \cong SU(3)/(SU(2)\times U(1)).
\]
This is a compact K\"ahler manifold with positive generator
\[
h=[\omega_{\mathrm{FS}}],
\qquad
\int_{\mathbb{CP}^1}h=1,
\qquad
\int_{\mathbb{CP}^2}h^2=1.
\]
\qed

\subsection{Theorem C: Microscopic origin of the rank-\(5\) split \(3+2\)}

\paragraph{Theorem C.}
Under hypotheses \textnormal{(H2)} and \textnormal{(H3)}, the internal defect zero-mode bundle is naturally
\[
V = E_3\oplus E_2,
\]
with
\[
E_3=L\otimes \underline{\mathbb C}^3,
\qquad
E_2=T^{1,0}\mathbb{CP}^2,
\]
where \(L\to\mathbb{CP}^2\) is the tautological line bundle.
In particular,
\[
\operatorname{rank}(E_3)=3,
\qquad
\operatorname{rank}(E_2)=2,
\]
and
\[
c_1(E_3)+c_1(E_2)=0.
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
The universal exact sequence on \(\mathbb{CP}^2\) is
\[
0\to L\to \underline{\mathbb C}^3\to Q\to 0.
\]
The tangent bundle is
\[
T^{1,0}\mathbb{CP}^2 \cong L^*\otimes Q,
\]
so the orientational deformation sector is naturally the rank-two bundle
\[
E_2:=T^{1,0}\mathbb{CP}^2.
\]
The ambient triplet sector must be corrected by projective covariance, giving
\[
E_3:=L\otimes \underline{\mathbb C}^3.
\]
Since \(c_1(L)=-h\) and \(c_1(T^{1,0}\mathbb{CP}^2)=3h\), one finds
\[
c_1(E_3)=3c_1(L)=-3h,
\qquad
c_1(E_2)=3h.
\]
Therefore
\[
c_1(V)=c_1(E_3)+c_1(E_2)=0.
\]
\qed

\subsection{Corollary D: Structure group reduction and hypercharge direction}

\paragraph{Corollary D.}
Under the assumptions of Theorem C, the structure group of \(V\) reduces from \(U(5)\) to
\[
S(U(3)\times U(2)),
\]
and the unique traceless central abelian generator is
\[
Y=\mathrm{diag}(2a,2a,2a,-3a,-3a).
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
Since
\[
c_1(V)=0,
\]
the determinant is trivial:
\[
\det V \cong \mathcal O.
\]
Hence the structure group reduces to \(S(U(3)\times U(2))\).
A central block-diagonal abelian generator has the form
\[
Y=\mathrm{diag}(y_3,y_3,y_3,y_2,y_2),
\]
and the tracelessness condition gives
\[
3y_3+2y_2=0.
\]
Thus
\[
y_3=2a,\qquad y_2=-3a,
\]
which yields the stated generator.
\qed

\subsection{Theorem E: Canonical family bundle and anomaly-free chiral family}

\paragraph{Theorem E.}
Under the assumptions of Theorem C and Corollary D, the canonical chiral family bundle
\[
\mathcal W=\overline V\oplus \Lambda^2V
\]
decomposes as
\[
(\mathbf 3,\mathbf 2)_a
\oplus
(\mathbf 1,\mathbf 2)_{-3a}
\oplus
(\overline{\mathbf 3},\mathbf 1)_{-4a}
\oplus
(\overline{\mathbf 3},\mathbf 1)_{2a}
\oplus
(\mathbf 1,\mathbf 1)_{6a}.
\]
If electric charge is normalized by
\[
Q=T_3+Y
\]
and the mixed doublet is required to carry charges
\[
\frac23,\quad -\frac13,
\]
then
\[
a=\frac16,
\]
and the resulting family is exactly one Standard Model family in left-handed notation.

\paragraph{Proof.}
Using
\[
V=E_3\oplus E_2,
\]
one has
\[
\overline V=E_3^*\oplus E_2^*,
\]
and
\[
\Lambda^2V
=
\Lambda^2E_3\oplus (E_3\otimes E_2)\oplus \Lambda^2E_2.
\]
The hypercharge generator of Corollary D determines the relative charges of these components, producing the stated decomposition.
The overall scale \(a\) is fixed by
\[
\frac12+a=\frac23,
\qquad
-\frac12+a=-\frac13,
\]
so
\[
a=\frac16.
\]
\qed

\paragraph{Proposition E'.}
The family bundle of Theorem E is anomaly-free:
\[
SU(3)^3=0,\quad
SU(3)^2U(1)=0,\quad
SU(2)^2U(1)=0,\quad
U(1)^3=0,\quad
\mathrm{grav}^2U(1)=0,
\]
and the global \(SU(2)\) anomaly vanishes.

\paragraph{Proof.}
Direct evaluation of the anomaly coefficients for
\[
(\mathbf 3,\mathbf 2)_{1/6}
\oplus
(\mathbf 1,\mathbf 2)_{-1/2}
\oplus
(\overline{\mathbf 3},\mathbf 1)_{-2/3}
\oplus
(\overline{\mathbf 3},\mathbf 1)_{1/3}
\oplus
(\mathbf 1,\mathbf 1)_{1}
\]
gives zero for all cubic and mixed perturbative anomalies.
The total number of \(SU(2)\) doublets is \(3+1=4\), which is even, so the Witten anomaly also vanishes.
\qed

\subsection{Theorem F: Chiral protection by index theory}

\paragraph{Theorem F.}
Under hypotheses \textnormal{(H2)} and \textnormal{(H3)}, chirality protection in the defect sector is governed by the index of a \(\mathrm{spin}^c\)-twisted Dirac operator on \(\mathbb{CP}^2\).

Let
\[
c_1(L_{\mathrm{spin}^c})=qh,\qquad q\in 2\mathbb Z+1,
\qquad
c_1(E)=mh.
\]
Then
\[
n_L-n_R
=
\mathrm{Index}\,D_+^{(L,E)}
=
\frac{(2m+q)^2-1}{8},
\]
up to orientation sign convention for the defect flux.

\paragraph{Proof.}
Since
\[
w_2(T\mathbb{CP}^2)\neq 0,
\]
\(\mathbb{CP}^2\) is not spin, but it is \(\mathrm{spin}^c\).
Applying the Atiyah--Singer index theorem to the twisted chiral Dirac operator yields
\[
\mathrm{Index}\,D_+^{(L,E)}
=
\int_{\mathbb{CP}^2}\hat A(T\mathbb{CP}^2)\,\mathrm{ch}(L^{1/2}\otimes E).
\]
Using
\[
\hat A(T\mathbb{CP}^2)=1-\frac18 h^2,
\qquad
\mathrm{ch}(L^{1/2}\otimes E)=e^{(m+q/2)h},
\]
one obtains
\[
\mathrm{Index}\,D_+^{(L,E)}
=
\frac{(2m+q)^2-1}{8}.
\]
Hence chirality is protected precisely when this index is nonzero.
\qed

\subsection{Theorem G: Generation number from geometric quantization}

\paragraph{Theorem G.}
Under hypothesis \textnormal{(H4)}, the generation Hilbert space is
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{fam}}
=
H^0(\mathbb{CP}^2,\mathcal O(1)),
\]
and therefore
\[
N_{\mathrm{gen}}
=
\dim H^0(\mathbb{CP}^2,\mathcal O(1))
=
3.
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
The defect moduli space is
\[
\mathcal M_{\mathrm{def}}\cong \mathbb{CP}^2,
\]
with prequantum line bundle
\[
\mathcal L_k=\mathcal O(k),
\qquad
c_1(\mathcal L_k)=kh.
\]
At minimal positive level \(k=1\), geometric quantization gives
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{fam}}=H^0(\mathbb{CP}^2,\mathcal O(1)).
\]
By Hirzebruch--Riemann--Roch,
\[
\chi(\mathbb{CP}^2,\mathcal O(k))
=
\frac{(k+1)(k+2)}{2}.
\]
Kodaira vanishing implies
\[
H^q(\mathbb{CP}^2,\mathcal O(1))=0
\qquad (q>0),
\]
so
\[
\dim H^0(\mathbb{CP}^2,\mathcal O(1))=\chi(\mathbb{CP}^2,\mathcal O(1))=3.
\]
\qed

\subsection{Corollary H: Three anomaly-free families}

\paragraph{Corollary H.}
Under the assumptions of Theorem E and Theorem G, the full chiral defect matter content is
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{tot}}
=
H^0(\mathbb{CP}^2,\mathcal O(1))\otimes \mathcal W
\cong
3\,\mathcal W,
\]
that is, exactly three copies of one anomaly-free Standard Model family.

\paragraph{Proof.}
Immediate from
\[
\dim H^0(\mathbb{CP}^2,\mathcal O(1))=3
\]
and the anomaly-freeness of \(\mathcal W\).
\qed

\subsection{Proposition I: Flavor hierarchy and mixing}

\paragraph{Proposition I.}
Assume the family space
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{fam}}\cong \mathbb C^3
\]
is lifted by sector-dependent effective mass operators
\[
H_f
=
m_{0,f}\mathbf 1_3
+
\lambda_f T^{(1)}(V_f)
+
\Delta_f^{\mathrm{np}},
\qquad
f\in\{u,d,e,\nu\},
\]
where \(T^{(1)}(V_f)\) is the Toeplitz quantization of a real anisotropy potential on \(\mathbb{CP}^2\), and \(\Delta_f^{\mathrm{np}}\) contains overlap/tunneling effects.
Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the three generations are degenerate in the exact \(\mathbb{CP}^2\)-symmetric limit and split when the BCC-induced anisotropy is included;
\item if the diagonal entries are controlled semiclassically by actions \(S_{f,i}\), then
\[
m_{f,i}\sim A_{f,i}e^{-S_{f,i}};
\]
\item the mixing matrices are
\[
V_{\mathrm{CKM}}=U_u^\dagger U_d,
\qquad
U_{\mathrm{PMNS}}=U_e^\dagger U_\nu,
\]
where
\[
U_f^\dagger H_f U_f=\mathrm{diag}(m_{f1},m_{f2},m_{f3}).
\]
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Proof.}
The generation Hilbert space is three-dimensional by Theorem G.
In the exact symmetric limit, its Hamiltonian is proportional to the identity.
Toeplitz quantization of a real anisotropy potential produces a Hermitian lifting operator, hence distinct family eigenvalues.
The overlap/tunneling ansatz yields exponential suppression of effective Yukawa couplings.
Basis mismatch between sectoral diagonalizations gives the standard mixing matrices.
\qed

\subsection{Proposition J: Neutrino branch structure}

\paragraph{Proposition J.}
In the minimal family bundle \(\mathcal W\), the left-handed neutrino is present automatically in
\[
(\mathbf 1,\mathbf 2)_{-1/2},
\]
but a neutral singlet
\[
(\mathbf 1,\mathbf 1)_0
\]
is not forced.
Therefore:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the minimal/default branch is Dirac, provided an additional sterile neutral partner exists and \(U(1)_L\) is preserved;
\item the Majorana/seesaw branch requires both a sterile neutral singlet and a \(\Delta L=2\) pairing channel.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Proof.}
This is a bundle-theoretic statement.
A Dirac mass requires a pairing between distinct neutral bundles, whereas a Majorana mass requires a self-pairing of a neutral bundle.
The minimal family geometry contains \(\nu_L\) but does not by itself force a sterile singlet or a lepton-number-violating self-pairing.
Hence Majorana is not the minimal/default option.
\qed

\subsection{Theorem K: IR isotropy of the TECT soft sector}

\paragraph{Theorem K.}
Under hypothesis \textnormal{(H5)}, the infrared soft sector of TECT is governed by an isotropic fixed point with conservative effective component number
\[
N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6.
\]
Then the leading quartic cubic anisotropy operator has RG eigenvalue
\[
\theta_\tau
=
\epsilon\left(\frac{4-N_{\mathrm{eff}}}{N_{\mathrm{eff}}+8}\right)
=
-\frac{\epsilon}{7}<0.
\]
Hence the quartic cubic anisotropy is irrelevant in the infrared.

If the derivative anisotropy and sectoral velocity-mismatch directions are also irrelevant, then the low-energy theory becomes spatially isotropic and exhibits velocity locking.
If temporal matching also occurs, emergent Lorentz invariance follows.

\paragraph{Proof.}
The TECT infrared truncation can be organized into a real multiplet
\[
\Phi=(A_1,A_2,n_1,n_2,\chi_1,\chi_2),
\qquad
N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6.
\]
The leading quartic anisotropy coupling \(g_{\tau,k}\) obeys
\[
\partial_t \tilde g_\tau
=
\theta_\tau \tilde g_\tau+\mathcal O(\tilde g_\tau^2),
\]
with
\[
\theta_\tau
=
\epsilon\left(\frac{4-N_{\mathrm{eff}}}{N_{\mathrm{eff}}+8}\right).
\]
Substituting \(N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6\) gives
\[
\theta_\tau=-\frac{\epsilon}{7}<0.
\]
Thus
\[
\tilde g_\tau(k)\to 0
\qquad (k\to 0).
\]
If the derivative anisotropy coupling and the velocity-mismatch variables also carry negative RG eigenvalues, they likewise flow to zero.
Hence the infrared theory becomes isotropic.
\qed

\subsection{Master theorem}

\paragraph{Master Theorem.}
Assume hypotheses \textnormal{(H1)}--\textnormal{(H5)}.
Then the TECT BCC condensate admits an infrared defect sector with the following mathematically organized structure:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the ultraviolet phase is selected by the exact BCC quartic resonance invariant
\[
\Lambda_{\mathrm{BCC}}=540;
\]

\item the internal orientational geometry is
\[
\mathbb{CP}^2;
\]

\item the internal defect zero-mode bundle is
\[
V=(L\otimes \underline{\mathbb C}^3)\oplus T^{1,0}\mathbb{CP}^2,
\]
with
\[
\operatorname{rank}(V)=5,
\qquad
c_1(V)=0;
\]

\item the structure group reduces to
\[
S(U(3)\times U(2)),
\]
with unique traceless central hypercharge direction
\[
Y\propto \mathrm{diag}(2,2,2,-3,-3);
\]

\item the canonical chiral family bundle
\[
\mathcal W=\overline V\oplus \Lambda^2V
\]
gives one anomaly-free Standard Model family after the normalization
\[
a=\frac16;
\]

\item the chiral asymmetry of defect zero modes is protected by the index of a \(\mathrm{spin}^c\)-twisted Dirac operator on \(\mathbb{CP}^2\);

\item geometric quantization of the minimally quantized defect moduli yields exactly
\[
N_{\mathrm{gen}}=3;
\]

\item the family hierarchy and mixing arise from BCC-induced lifting of the common generation Hilbert space and sector-dependent overlap/tunneling operators;

\item the microscopic cubic anisotropy of the BCC phase is infrared-irrelevant, so the TECT low-energy theory flows to an isotropic continuum fixed point, and with temporal matching, to an emergent Lorentzian sector.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore, within the stated hypotheses, TECT admits an internally consistent infrared structure reproducing the algebraic and representation-theoretic skeleton of
\[
SU(3)_c\times SU(2)_L\times U(1)_Y
\]
with three chiral anomaly-free families, flavor structure, and infrared isotropy.

\subsection{What is established versus what remains open}

The theorem chain above establishes the following at the structural level:

\begin{enumerate}
\item exact ultraviolet BCC selection through \(\Lambda_{\mathrm{BCC}}=540\),
\item the \(\mathbb{CP}^2\) internal geometry,
\item the rank-\(5\) split \(3+2\),
\item the hypercharge direction and family bundle,
\item anomaly cancellation,
\item the index-theoretic chirality criterion,
\item the generation count \(N_{\mathrm{gen}}=3\),
\item the general geometric origin of hierarchy and mixing,
\item the RG mechanism of infrared isotropy.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is not the abstract structure of the chain, but its strongest analytic and dynamical completion:

\begin{enumerate}
\item deriving the full defect PDE spectrum and proving the zero-mode sector without adiabatic truncation,
\item proving dynamically that the physically realized family bundle is exactly \(\overline V\oplus \Lambda^2V\),
\item deriving the microscopic anisotropy potentials and overlap actions that reproduce the observed masses and mixing angles quantitatively,
\item deriving or excluding sterile neutral modes and deciding dynamically between the Dirac and Majorana neutrino branches,
\item performing a fully TECT-specific functional RG computation beyond schematic one-loop order.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the present results should be read as a mathematically organized theorem chain for the infrared Standard-Model-type sector of TECT, rather than as the final closure of every microscopic dynamical detail.

\section{Compressed master summary}

Assuming:

\[
\text{(i) BCC ultraviolet selection by } \Lambda_{\mathrm{BCC}}=540,
\]
\[
\text{(ii) projective internal order parameter } z\sim e^{i\alpha}z \in \mathbb C^3,
\]
\[
\text{(iii) localized defect reduction to } \mathbb{CP}^2,
\]
\[
\text{(iv) minimal positive moduli quantization level } k=1,
\]
\[
\text{(v) infrared isotropic fixed point with } N_{\mathrm{eff}}=6,
\]

one obtains the chain

\[
\Lambda_{\mathrm{BCC}}=540
\Longrightarrow
\mathbb{CP}^2
\Longrightarrow
V=(L\otimes \underline{\mathbb C}^3)\oplus T^{1,0}\mathbb{CP}^2
\Longrightarrow
c_1(V)=0
\]
\[
\Longrightarrow
S(U(3)\times U(2))
\Longrightarrow
Y\propto \mathrm{diag}(2,2,2,-3,-3)
\Longrightarrow
\mathcal W=\overline V\oplus \Lambda^2V
\]
\[
\Longrightarrow
\text{one anomaly-free Standard Model family}
\Longrightarrow
H^0(\mathbb{CP}^2,\mathcal O(1))\cong \mathbb C^3
\Longrightarrow
N_{\mathrm{gen}}=3
\]
\[
\Longrightarrow
\text{sector-dependent lifting } \Rightarrow \text{hierarchy and mixing}
\Longrightarrow
\theta_\tau
=
\epsilon\frac{4-6}{14}
=
-\frac{\epsilon}{7}<0
\Longrightarrow
\text{IR isotropy}.
\]

Hence, under the stated hypotheses, TECT reproduces the structural infrared skeleton of a three-family chiral anomaly-free
\[
SU(3)_c\times SU(2)_L\times U(1)_Y
\]
theory together with flavor structure and an isotropic low-energy continuum limit.
